  The data value contained in the first record that satisifes the given predicate will be bound to the global scope. Otherwise if no records match, then no value will be bound.

  <p>Examples</p>

  ### CSV Lookup

  Given the CSV file: lookup/StateCodes.csv

  ```csv {9}
  Code,Name
  ACT,Australian Capital Territory
  NSW,New South Wales
  NT,Northern Territory
  QLD,Queensland
  SA,South Australia
  TAS,Tasmania
  VIC,Victoria
  WA,Western Australia
  ```

  The following will bind "Western Australia" in the last record to <code>Name</code> in the global scope

  ```gherkin {1}
    When I lookup Name in the "lookup/StateCodes.csv" file where "'${data.record.Code}' == 'WA'"
    Then Name should be "Western Australia"
  ```

  ### JSON Lookup
 
  > Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v3.47.0">v3.47.0</Link>

  Given the JSON file: lookup/StateCodes.json

  ```json {5}
  [
    { "Code": "ACT", "Name": "Australian Capital Territory" },
    { "Code": "NSW", "Name": "New South Wales" },
    { "Code": "NT",  "Name": "Northern Territory" },
    { "Code": "QLD", "Name": "Queensland" },
    { "Code": "SA",  "Name": "South Australia" },
    { "Code": "TAS", "Name": "Tasmania" },
    { "Code": "VIC", "Name": "Victoria" },
    { "Code": "WA",  "Name": "Western Australia" }
  ]
  ```

  The following will bind "Western Australia" in the last record to <code>Name</code> in the global scope

  ```gherkin {1}
    When I lookup Name in the "lookup/StateCodes.json" file where "'${data.record.Code}' == 'WA'"
    Then Name should be "Western Australia"
  ```

  <div class="grid-3">
    <div><Link to="#i-lookup-name-in-the-filepath-file-where-filter">Link</Link></div>
    <div align="center"></div>
    <div align="right">Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v3.30.0">v3.30.0</Link></div>
  </div>
</details>

<details id="i-lookup-name-in-the-filepath-ref-file-where-filter">
  <summary class="dsl">

  ```gherkin
  I lookup <name> in <filepathRef> file where "<predicate>"
  ```
  <p>Looks up a named data value in a referenced CSV or JSON file based on a predicate function and binds its value to the same name in the global scope.</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;name&gt;</code>the name of the data to look up the value of and the name to bind it to</li>
    <li><code>&lt;filepathRef&gt;</code> is the name of the binding containing the path of the CSV or JSON file to look up</li>
    <li><code>&lt;predicate&gt;</code> is the javascript predicate expression or anonymous function that will return <code>true</code> when a match is found for a record or <code>false</code> otherwise (can be in <Link to="/docs/advanced/doc-strings">DocString</Link> position)
      <ul>
        <li>For an expression: no <code>return</code> prefix is required</li>
        <li>For an anonymous function: the syntax is <code>(function()&#123; body &#125;)()</code> where body must return a value</li>
      </ul>
      Data fields can be referenced in the predicate using either:
      <ul>
        <li><code>$&#123;data.record.NAME&#125;</code> (since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v3.47.0">v3.47.0</Link>)</li>
        <li><code>$&#123;csv.record.NAME&#125;</code> for CSV data or <code>$&#123;json.record.NAME&#125;</code> for JSON data (for prior versions)</li>
      </ul>
    </li>
  </ul>

  The data value contained in the first record that satisifes the given predicate will be bound to the global scope. Otherwise if no records match, then no value will be bound.

  <p>Examples</p>

  ### CSV Lookup

  Given the CSV file: lookup/StateCodes.csv

  ```csv {5}
  Code,Name
  ACT,Australian Capital Territory
  NSW,New South Wales
  NT,Northern Territory
  QLD,Queensland
  SA,South Australia
  TAS,Tasmania
  VIC,Victoria
  WA,Western Australia
  ```

  The following will bind "QLD" in the 4th record to <code>Code</code> in the global scope

  ```gherkin {2}
    Given mapping file is "lookup/StateCodes.csv"
     When I lookup Code in mapping file where "'${data.record.Name}' == 'Queensland'"
     Then Code should be "QLD"
  ```

  ### JSON Lookup
 
  > Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v3.47.0">v3.47.0</Link>

  Given the JSON file: lookup/StateCodes.json

  ```json {5}
  [
    { "Code": "ACT", "Name": "Australian Capital Territory" },
    { "Code": "NSW", "Name": "New South Wales" },
    { "Code": "NT",  "Name": "Northern Territory" },
    { "Code": "QLD", "Name": "Queensland" },
    { "Code": "SA",  "Name": "South Australia" },
    { "Code": "TAS", "Name": "Tasmania" },
    { "Code": "VIC", "Name": "Victoria" },
    { "Code": "WA",  "Name": "Western Australia" }
  ]
  ```

  The following will bind "QLD" in the 4th record to <code>Code</code> in the global scope

  ```gherkin {2}
    Given mapping file is "lookup/StateCodes.json"
     When I lookup Code in mapping file where "'${data.record.Name}' == 'Queensland'"
     Then Code should be "QLD"
  ```

  <div class="grid-3">
    <div><Link to="#i-lookup-name-in-the-filepath-ref-file-where-filter">Link</Link></div>
    <div align="center"></div>
    <div align="right">Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v3.30.0">v3.30.0</Link></div>
  </div>
</details>

<details id="i-lookup-column-in-the-filepath-file-as-name-where-filter">
  <summary class="dsl">

  ```gherkin
  I lookup <dataName> in the "<filepath>" file as <name> where "<predicate>"
  ```
  <p>Looks up a named data value in a CSV or JSON file based on a predicate function and binds its value to a given name in the global scope.</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;dataName&gt;</code> the name of the data to look up the value of</li>
    <li><code>&lt;filepath&gt;</code> the path to the CSV or JSON file to look up</li>
    <li><code>&lt;name&gt;</code> the name to bind the looked up value to in the global scope</li>
    <li><code>&lt;predicate&gt;</code> is the javascript predicate expression or anonymous function that will return <code>true</code> when a match is found for a record or <code>false</code> otherwise (can be in <Link to="/docs/advanced/doc-strings">DocString</Link> position)
      <ul>
        <li>For an expression: no <code>return</code> prefix is required</li>
        <li>For an anonymous function: the syntax is <code>(function()&#123; body &#125;)()</code> where body must return a value</li>
      </ul>
      Data fields can be referenced in the predicate using either:
      <ul>
        <li><code>$&#123;data.record.NAME&#125;</code> (since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v3.47.0">v3.47.0</Link>)</li>
        <li><code>$&#123;csv.record.NAME&#125;</code> for CSV data or <code>$&#123;json.record.NAME&#125;</code> for JSON data (for prior versions)</li>
      </ul>
    </li>
  </ul>

  The data value contained in the first record that satisifes the given predicate will be bound to the global scope. Otherwise if no records match, then no value will be bound.

  <p>Examples</p>

  ### CSV Lookup

  Given the CSV file: lookup/StateCodes.csv

  ```csv {3}
  Code,Name
  ACT,Australian Capital Territory
  NSW,New South Wales
  NT,Northern Territory
  QLD,Queensland
  SA,South Australia
  TAS,Tasmania
  VIC,Victoria
  WA,Western Australia
  ```

  The following will bind "New South Wales" in the 2nd record to <code>state name</code> in the global scope

  ```gherkin {1}
    When I lookup Name in the "lookup/StateCodes.csv" file as state name where "'${data.record.Code}' == 'NSW'"
    Then state name should be "New South Wales"
  ```

  ### JSON Lookup
 
  > Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v3.47.0">v3.47.0</Link>

  Given the JSON file: lookup/StateCodes.json

  ```json {5}
  [
    { "Code": "ACT", "Name": "Australian Capital Territory" },
    { "Code": "NSW", "Name": "New South Wales" },
    { "Code": "NT",  "Name": "Northern Territory" },
    { "Code": "QLD", "Name": "Queensland" },
    { "Code": "SA",  "Name": "South Australia" },
    { "Code": "TAS", "Name": "Tasmania" },
    { "Code": "VIC", "Name": "Victoria" },
    { "Code": "WA",  "Name": "Western Australia" }
  ]
  ```

  The following will bind "New South Wales" in the 2nd record to <code>state name</code> in the global scope

  ```gherkin {1}
    When I lookup Name in the "lookup/StateCodes.json" file as state name where "'${data.record.Code}' == 'NSW'"
    Then state name should be "New South Wales"
  ```

  <div class="grid-3">
    <div><Link to="#i-lookup-column-in-the-filepath-file-as-name-where-filter">Link</Link></div>
    <div align="center"></div>
    <div align="right">Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v3.30.0">v3.30.0</Link></div>
  </div>
</details>

<details id="i-lookup-column-in-the-filepath-ref-file-as-name-where-filter">
  <summary class="dsl">

  ```gherkin
  I lookup <dataName> in <filepathRef> file as <name> where "<predicate>"
  ```
  <p>Looks up a named column value in a referenced CSV or JSON file based on a predicate function and binds its value to a given name in the global scope.</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;dataName&gt;</code> the name of the data in the CSV or JSON file to look up the value of</li>
    <li><code>&lt;filepathRef&gt;</code> is the name of the binding containing the path of the CSV or JSON file to look up</li>
    <li><code>&lt;name&gt;</code> the name to bind the looked up value to in the global scope</li>
    <li><code>&lt;predicate&gt;</code> is the javascript predicate expression or anonymous function that will return <code>true</code> when a match is found for a record or <code>false</code> otherwise (can be in <Link to="/docs/advanced/doc-strings">DocString</Link> position)
      <ul>
        <li>For an expression: no <code>return</code> prefix is required</li>
        <li>For an anonymous function: the syntax is <code>(function()&#123; body &#125;)()</code> where body must return a value</li>
      </ul>
      Data fields can be referenced in the predicate using either:
      <ul>
        <li><code>$&#123;data.record.NAME&#125;</code> (since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v3.47.0">v3.47.0</Link>)</li>
        <li><code>$&#123;csv.record.NAME&#125;</code> for CSV data or <code>$&#123;json.record.NAME&#125;</code> for JSON data (for prior versions)</li>
      </ul>
    </li>
  </ul>

  The data value contained in the first record that satisifes the given predicate will be bound to the global scope. Otherwise if no records match, then no value will be bound.

  <p>Examples</p>

  ### CSV Lookup

  Given the CSV file: lookup/StateCodes.csv

  ```csv {8}
  Code,Name
  ACT,Australian Capital Territory
  NSW,New South Wales
  NT,Northern Territory
  QLD,Queensland
  SA,South Australia
  TAS,Tasmania
  VIC,Victoria
  WA,Western Australia
  ```

  The following will bind "VIC" in the 7th record to <code>state code</code> in the global scope

  ```gherkin {2}
    Given mapping file is "lookup/StateCodes.csv"
     When I lookup Code in mapping file as state code where "'${data.record.Name}' == 'Victoria'"
     Then state code should be "VIC"
  ```

  ### JSON Lookup
 
  > Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v3.47.0">v3.47.0</Link>

  Given the JSON file: lookup/StateCodes.json

  ```json {5}
  [
    { "Code": "ACT", "Name": "Australian Capital Territory" },
    { "Code": "NSW", "Name": "New South Wales" },
    { "Code": "NT",  "Name": "Northern Territory" },
    { "Code": "QLD", "Name": "Queensland" },
    { "Code": "SA",  "Name": "South Australia" },
    { "Code": "TAS", "Name": "Tasmania" },
    { "Code": "VIC", "Name": "Victoria" },
    { "Code": "WA",  "Name": "Western Australia" }
  ]
  ```

  The following will bind "VIC" in the 7th record to <code>state code</code> in the global scope

  ```gherkin {2}
    Given mapping file is "lookup/StateCodes.json"
     When I lookup Code in mapping file as state code where "'${data.record.Name}' == 'Victoria'"
     Then state code should be "VIC"
  ```

  <div class="grid-3">
    <div><Link to="#i-lookup-column-in-the-filepath-ref-file-as-name-where-filter">Link</Link></div>
    <div align="center"></div>
    <div align="right">Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v3.30.0">v3.30.0</Link></div>
  </div>
</details>

## SQL selects and updates

### Given

<details id="name-is-defined-by-database-select-statement">
  <summary class="dsl">

  ```gherkin
  <name> is defined in the <dbName> database by sql "<selectStmt>"
  ```
  
  <p>Associates the result of an SQL database query to the given name in the global scope. The value is resolved every time the name is referenced.</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;name&gt;</code> is the name to bind the SQL query result to</li>
    <li><code>&lt;dbName&gt;</code> the name of the configured database to execute the query on</li>
    <li><code>&lt;selectStmt&gt;</code> is the SQL query that will return the value to assign (can be in <Link to="/docs/advanced/doc-strings">DocString</Link> position)</li>
  </ul>

  <p>Configuration</p>
  <ul>
    <li>The `GWEN_CLASSPATH` environment variable must be set to include a path to the JDBC driver JAR</li>
    <li>A <code>gwen.db.&lt;dbName&gt;.driver</code> setting must be set to the name of the JDBC driver implementation class</li>
    <li>A <code>gwen.db.&lt;dbName&gt;.url</code> setting must be set to the JDBC URL of the database</li>
  </ul>

  <p>
    Optionally accepts the <Link href="/docs/advanced/eager-or-lazy"><code>@Eager</code> or <code>@Lazy</code></Link> annotations.
    <ul>
      <li><code>@Eager</code> immediately evaluates the <code>&lt;expression&gt;</code> and binds the result to <code>&lt;name&gt;</code></li>
      <li><code>@Lazy</code> evaluates the <code>&lt;expression&gt;</code> and binds the result to <code>&lt;name&gt;</code> when it is first referenced</li>
      <li>In the absence of either annotation, <code>&lt;expression&gt;</code> is evaluated every time <code>&lt;name&gt;</code> is referenced</li>
    </ul>
  </p>

  <p>Example</p>

  ```gherkin {1-4}
    Given the email address is defined in the feedback database by sql
          """
          select email from comments
          """
     Then the email address should be "some.person@example.com"
  ```

<Tabs
  groupId="setup"
  defaultValue="linux"
  values={[
    {label: 'Linux', value: 'linux'},
    {label: 'Windows', value: 'windows'},
  ]}>
  
<TabItem value="linux">

  Set GWEN_CLASSPATH variable in the environment to include the JDBC driver JAR

  ```shell
  export GWEN_CLASSPATH=/path-to-driver/mysql-connector-java-5.1.40-bin.jar
  ```

</TabItem>
<TabItem value="windows">

  Set GWEN_CLASSPATH variable in the environment to include the JDBC driver JAR

  ```shell
  set GWEN_CLASSPATH c:/path-to-driver/mysql-connector-java-5.1.40-bin.jar
  ```

</TabItem>
</Tabs>

  Configure the database in your settings. In this example, <code>&lt;dbName&gt;</code>=feedback

  ```properties
  gwen.db.feedback.driver = com.mysql.jdbc.Driver
  gwen.db.feedback.url = jdbc:mysql://localhost/feedback?user=myUser&amp;password=myPassword&amp;
  ```

  <div class="grid-3">
    <div><Link to="#name-is-defined-by-database-select-statement">Link</Link></div>
    <div align="center"><Link to="https://gweninterpreter.wordpress.com/2017/02/13/sql-data-bindings-for-gwen">Learn more</Link></div>
    <div align="right">Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.10.0">v2.10.0</Link></div>
  </div>
</details>

### When

<details id="i-update-database-by-sql-update-statement">
  <summary class="dsl">

  ```gherkin
  I update the <dbName> database by sql "<updateStmt>"
  ```
  <p>Executes an SQL udpate statement on a configured database.</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;dbName&gt;</code> the name of the configured database to run the update statement on</li>
    <li><code>&lt;updateStmt&gt;</code> is the SQL update statement to execute (can be in <Link to="/docs/advanced/doc-strings">DocString</Link> position)</li>
  </ul>

  <p>Returns</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;dbName&gt; rows affected</code> = the number of rows affected by the update</li>
  </ul>

  <p>Configuration</p>
  <ul>
    <li>The `GWEN_CLASSPATH` environment variable must be set to include a path to the JDBC driver JAR</li>
    <li>A <code>gwen.db.&lt;dbName&gt;.driver</code> setting must be set to the name of the JDBC driver implementation class</li>
    <li>A <code>gwen.db.&lt;dbName&gt;.url</code> setting must be set to the JDBC URL of the database</li>
  </ul>

  <p>Example</p>

  ```gherkin
    When I update the feedback database by sql
         """
         update comments set email='new@example.com' where email='old@example.com'
         """
    Then feedback rows affected should be "1"
  ```

  <Tabs
  groupId="setup"
  defaultValue="linux"
  values={[
    {label: 'Linux', value: 'linux'},
    {label: 'Windows', value: 'windows'},
  ]}>

<TabItem value="linux">

  Set GWEN_CLASSPATH variable in the environment to include the JDBC driver JAR

  ```shell
  export GWEN_CLASSPATH=/path-to-driver/mysql-connector-java-5.1.40-bin.jar
  ```

</TabItem>
<TabItem value="windows">

  Set GWEN_CLASSPATH variable in the environment to include the JDBC driver JAR

  ```shell
  set GWEN_CLASSPATH c:/path-to-driver/mysql-connector-java-5.1.40-bin.jar
  ```

</TabItem>
</Tabs>

  Configure the database in your settings. In this example, <code>&lt;dbName&gt;</code>=feedback

  ```properties
  gwen.db.feedback.driver = com.mysql.jdbc.Driver
  gwen.db.feedback.url = jdbc:mysql://localhost/feedback?user=myUser&amp;password=myPassword&amp;
  ```

  <div class="grid-3">
    <div><Link to="#i-update-database-by-sql-update-statement">Link</Link></div>
    <div align="center"><Link to="https://gweninterpreter.wordpress.com/2017/02/13/sql-data-bindings-for-gwen">Learn more</Link></div>
    <div align="right">Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.12.0">v2.12.0</Link></div>
  </div>
</details>

## Settings overrides

### Given

<details id="my-name-setting-is-value">
  <summary class="dsl">

  ```gherkin
  my <name> setting is "<value>"
  ```
  <p> Overrides a Gwen setting.</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;name&gt;</code> is name of the setting to override</li>
    <li><code>&lt;value&gt;</code> is the value to set</li>
  </ul>
  <p>Notes</p>
  <ul>
    <li>Or as of <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.21.0">v2.21.0</Link>, this DSL stores all values as thread local settings (instead of system properties).
      <ul>
        <li>This supports different settings for different features in the case of parallel execution.</li>
        <li>Settings loaded from properties files and system properties at startup time are not replaced, but can be overridden with values set here.</li>
        <li>Setting arbitrary system properties (that is: non Gwen settings that do not start with <code>gwen.</code>) is not supported.</li>
      </ul>
    </li>
    <li>Prior to <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.21.0">v2.21.0</Link>, this DSL stored all values as JVM-global system properties and caution was advised because race conditions could occur if multiple features changed the same system property.</li>
  </ul>
  <p>Example</p>

  ```gherkin
    Given my gwen.web.useragent setting is "I am robot"
  ```

  <div class="grid-3">
    <div><Link to="#my-name-setting-is-value">Link</Link></div>
    <div align="center"></div>
    <div align="right">Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v1.0.0">v1.0.0</Link></div>
  </div>
</details>

<details id="i-reset-my-name-setting">
  <summary class="dsl">

  ```gherkin
  I reset my <name> setting
  ```
  <p> Resets a Gwen setting to remove a previous override.</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;setting&gt;</code> is name of the setting to reset</li>
  </ul>
  <p>Example</p>

  ```gherkin
    Given I reset my gwen.web.useragent setting
  ```

  <div class="grid-3">
    <div><Link to="#i-reset-my-name-setting">Link</Link></div>
    <div align="center"></div>
    <div align="right">Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.21.0">v2.21.0</Link></div>
  </div>
</details>

## Control structures

### ForEach

> Since [v3.48.0](https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v3.47.0), the following implicit attributes are available to <code>&lt;step&gt;</code>s:
> <ul>
>  <li><code>iteration.number</code> = current iteration starting at 1</li>
>  <li><code>iteration.index</code> = current iteration starting at 0</li>
> </ul>

<details id="step-for-each-element-located-by-selector-expression">
  <summary class="dsl">

  ```gherkin
  <step> for each <element> located by <selector> "<expression>"
  ```
  <p>Executes a step for each element in a list of elements in the current scope with a default lookup timeout.</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;step&gt;</code> is the DSL step or StepDef to execute for each element</li>
    <li><code>&lt;element&gt;</code> is the name that will be assigned to the current element occurrence (element is accessible in <code>&lt;step&gt;</code> by this name)</li>
    <li><code>&lt;selector&gt;</code> is the selector type, one of:
      <ul>
        <li><code>id</code> for selecting by id attribute</li>
        <li><code>name</code> for selecting by name attribute</li>
        <li><code>tag name</code> (or <code>tag</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.46.0">v2.46.0</Link>) for selecting by tag name</li>
        <li><code>css selector</code> (or <code>css</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.46.0">v2.46.0</Link>) for selecting by css expression</li>
        <li><code>class name</code> (or <code>class</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.46.0">v2.46.0</Link>) for selecting by class attribute</li>
        <li><code>xpath</code> for selecting by XPath</li>
        <li><code>link text</code> for selecting by link text</li>
        <li><code>partial link text</code> for selecting by partial link text</li>
        <li><code>javascript</code> (or <code>js</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.46.0">v2.46.0</Link>) for selecting <Link to="https://gweninterpreter.wordpress.com/2019/08/13/locating-web-elements-with-gwen/#byJavaScript">by JavaScript</Link></li>
      </ul>
    </li>
    <li><code>&lt;expression&gt;</code> is the selector expression returning one or many elements</li>
  </ul>
  <p>Example</p>

  ```gherkin {6}
    Given the todo field can be located by class "new-todo"
      And the active count can be located by css ".todo-count strong"
     When I navigate to "https://todomvc.com/examples/react"
      And I enter "Walk the dog" in the todo field
      And I enter "Feed the cat" in the todo field
      And I tick todo item for each todo item located by css ".todo-list .toggle"
     Then the active count should be "0"
  ```

  <div class="grid-3">
    <div><Link to="#step-for-each-element-located-by-selector-expression">Link</Link></div>
    <div align="center"></div>
    <div align="right">Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.4.0">v2.4.0</Link></div>
  </div>
</details>

<details id="step-for-each-element-located-by-selector-expression-with-no-timeout">
  <summary class="dsl">

  ```gherkin
  <step> for each <element> located by <selector> "<expression>" with no <wait|timeout>
  ```
  <p>Executes a step for each element in a list of elements in the current scope with a no lookup timeout.</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;step&gt;</code> is the DSL step or StepDef to execute for each element</li>
    <li><code>&lt;element&gt;</code> is the name that will be assigned to the current element occurrence (element is accessible in <code>&lt;step&gt;</code> by this name)</li>
    <li><code>&lt;selector&gt;</code> is the selector type, one of:
      <ul>
        <li><code>id</code> for selecting by id attribute</li>
        <li><code>name</code> for selecting by name attribute</li>
        <li><code>tag name</code> (or <code>tag</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.46.0">v2.46.0</Link>) for selecting by tag name</li>
        <li><code>css selector</code> (or <code>css</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.46.0">v2.46.0</Link>) for selecting by css expression</li>
        <li><code>class name</code> (or <code>class</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.46.0">v2.46.0</Link>) for selecting by class attribute</li>
        <li><code>xpath</code> for selecting by XPath</li>
        <li><code>link text</code> for selecting by link text</li>
        <li><code>partial link text</code> for selecting by partial link text</li>
        <li><code>javascript</code> (or <code>js</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.46.0">v2.46.0</Link>) for selecting <Link to="https://gweninterpreter.wordpress.com/2019/08/13/locating-web-elements-with-gwen/#byJavaScript">by JavaScript</Link></li>
      </ul>
    </li>
    <li><code>&lt;expression&gt;</code> is the selector expression returning one or many elements</li>
    <li><code>&lt;wait|timeout&gt;</code> is either <code>wait</code> or <code>timeout</code></li>
  </ul>
  <p>Example</p>

  ```gherkin {6}
    Given the todo field can be located by class "new-todo"
      And the active count can be located by css ".todo-count strong"
     When I navigate to "https://todomvc.com/examples/react"
      And I enter "Walk the dog" in the todo field
      And I enter "Feed the cat" in the todo field
      And I tick todo item for each todo item located by css ".todo-list .toggle" with no wait
     Then the active count should be "0"
  ```

  <div class="grid-3">
    <div><Link to="#step-for-each-element-located-by-selector-expression-with-no-timeout">Link</Link></div>
    <div align="center"></div>
    <div align="right">Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.19.0">v2.19.0</Link></div>
  </div>
</details>

<details id="step-for-each-element-located-by-selector-expression-with-timeout">
  <summary class="dsl">

  ```gherkin
  <step> for each <element> located by <selector> "<expression>" with <timeoutSecs> second <wait|timeout>
  ```
  <p>Executes a step for each element in a list of elements in the current scope with a given lookup timeout.</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;step&gt;</code> is the DSL step or StepDef to execute for each element</li>
    <li><code>&lt;element&gt;</code> is the name that will be assigned to the current element occurrence (element is accessible in <code>&lt;step&gt;</code> by this name)</li>
    <li><code>&lt;selector&gt;</code> is the selector type, one of:
      <ul>
        <li><code>id</code> for selecting by id attribute</li>
        <li><code>name</code> for selecting by name attribute</li>
        <li><code>tag name</code> (or <code>tag</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.46.0">v2.46.0</Link>) for selecting by tag name</li>
        <li><code>css selector</code> (or <code>css</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.46.0">v2.46.0</Link>) for selecting by css expression</li>
        <li><code>class name</code> (or <code>class</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.46.0">v2.46.0</Link>) for selecting by class attribute</li>
        <li><code>xpath</code> for selecting by XPath</li>
        <li><code>link text</code> for selecting by link text</li>
        <li><code>partial link text</code> for selecting by partial link text</li>
        <li><code>javascript</code> (or <code>js</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.46.0">v2.46.0</Link>) for selecting <Link to="https://gweninterpreter.wordpress.com/2019/08/13/locating-web-elements-with-gwen/#byJavaScript">by JavaScript</Link></li>
      </ul>
    </li>
    <li><code>&lt;expression&gt;</code> is the selector expression returning one or many elements</li>
    <li><code>&lt;timeoutSecs&gt;</code> is the timeout period in seconds</li>
    <li><code>&lt;wait|timeout&gt;</code> is either <code>wait</code> or <code>timeout</code></li>
  </ul>
  <p>Example</p>

  ```gherkin {6}
    Given the todo field can be located by class "new-todo"
      And the active count can be located by css ".todo-count strong"
     When I navigate to "https://todomvc.com/examples/react"
      And I enter "Walk the dog" in the todo field
      And I enter "Feed the cat" in the todo field
      And I tick todo item for each todo item located by css ".todo-list .toggle" with 5 second timeout
     Then the active count should be "0"
  ```

  <div class="grid-3">
    <div><Link to="#step-for-each-element-located-by-selector-expression-with-timeout">Link</Link></div>
    <div align="center"></div>
    <div align="right">Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.19.0">v2.19.0</Link></div>
  </div>
</details>

<details id="step-for-each-element-located-by-selector-expression-in-container">
  <summary class="dsl">

  ```gherkin
  <step> for each <element> located by <selector> "<expression>" in <containerElement>
  ```
  <p>Executes a step for each element in a list of elements in a container element in the current scope with a default lookup timeout.</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;step&gt;</code> is the DSL step or StepDef to execute for each element</li>
    <li><code>&lt;element&gt;</code> is the name that will be assigned to the current element occurrence (element is accessible in <code>&lt;step&gt;</code> by this name)</li>
    <li><code>&lt;selector&gt;</code> is the selector type, one of:
      <ul>
        <li><code>id</code> for selecting by id attribute</li>
        <li><code>name</code> for selecting by name attribute</li>
        <li><code>tag name</code> (or <code>tag</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.46.0">v2.46.0</Link>) for selecting by tag name</li>
        <li><code>css selector</code> (or <code>css</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.46.0">v2.46.0</Link>) for selecting by css expression</li>
        <li><code>class name</code> (or <code>class</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.46.0">v2.46.0</Link>) for selecting by class attribute</li>
        <li><code>xpath</code> for selecting by XPath</li>
        <li><code>link text</code> for selecting by link text</li>
        <li><code>partial link text</code> for selecting by partial link text</li>
        <li><code>javascript</code> (or <code>js</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.46.0">v2.46.0</Link>) for selecting <Link to="https://gweninterpreter.wordpress.com/2019/08/13/locating-web-elements-with-gwen/#byJavaScript">by JavaScript</Link></li>
      </ul>
    </li>
    <li><code>&lt;expression&gt;</code> is the selector expression returning one or many elements</li>
    <li><code>&lt;containerElement&gt;</code> is the name assigned to the container element</li>
  </ul>
  <p>Example</p>

  ```gherkin {7}
    Given the todo field can be located by class "new-todo"
      And the todo list can be located by class "todo-list"
      And the active count can be located by css ".todo-count strong"
     When I navigate to "https://todomvc.com/examples/react"
      And I enter "Walk the dog" in the todo field
      And I enter "Feed the cat" in the todo field
      And I tick todo item for each todo item located by class "toggle" in the todo list
     Then the active count should be "0"
  ```

  <div class="grid-3">
    <div><Link to="#step-for-each-element-located-by-selector-expression-in-container">Link</Link></div>
    <div align="center"></div>
    <div align="right">Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.4.0">v2.4.0</Link></div>
  </div>
</details>

<details id="step-for-each-element-located-by-selector-expression-in-container-with-no-timeout">
  <summary class="dsl">

  ```gherkin
  <step> for each <element> located by <selector> "<expression>" in <containerElement> with no <wait|timeout>
  ```
  <p>Executes a step for each element in a list of elements in a container element in the current scope with no lookup timeout.</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;step&gt;</code> is the DSL step or StepDef to execute for each element</li>
    <li><code>&lt;element&gt;</code> is the name that will be assigned to the current element occurrence (element is accessible in <code>&lt;step&gt;</code> by this name)</li>
    <li><code>&lt;selector&gt;</code> is the selector type, one of:
      <ul>
        <li><code>id</code> for selecting by id attribute</li>
        <li><code>name</code> for selecting by name attribute</li>
        <li><code>tag name</code> (or <code>tag</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.46.0">v2.46.0</Link>) for selecting by tag name</li>
        <li><code>css selector</code> (or <code>css</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.46.0">v2.46.0</Link>) for selecting by css expression</li>
        <li><code>class name</code> (or <code>class</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.46.0">v2.46.0</Link>) for selecting by class attribute</li>
        <li><code>xpath</code> for selecting by XPath</li>
        <li><code>link text</code> for selecting by link text</li>
        <li><code>partial link text</code> for selecting by partial link text</li>
        <li><code>javascript</code> (or <code>js</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.46.0">v2.46.0</Link>) for selecting <Link to="https://gweninterpreter.wordpress.com/2019/08/13/locating-web-elements-with-gwen/#byJavaScript">by JavaScript</Link></li>
      </ul>
    </li>
    <li><code>&lt;expression&gt;</code> is the selector expression returning one or many elements</li>
    <li><code>&lt;containerElement&gt;</code> is the name assigned to the container element</li>
    <li><code>&lt;wait|timeout&gt;</code> is either <code>wait</code> or <code>timeout</code></li>
  </ul>
  <p>Example</p>

  ```gherkin {7}
    Given the todo field can be located by class "new-todo"
      And the todo list can be located by class "todo-list"
      And the active count can be located by css ".todo-count strong"
     When I navigate to "https://todomvc.com/examples/react"
      And I enter "Walk the dog" in the todo field
      And I enter "Feed the cat" in the todo field
      And I tick todo item for each todo item located by class "toggle" in the todo list with no timeout
     Then the active count should be "0"
  ```

  <div class="grid-3">
    <div><Link to="#step-for-each-element-located-by-selector-expression-in-container-with-no-timeout">Link</Link></div>
    <div align="center"></div>
    <div align="right">Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.19.0">v2.19.0</Link></div>
  </div>
</details>

<details id="step-for-each-element-located-by-selector-expression-in-container-with-timeout">
  <summary class="dsl">

  ```gherkin
  <step> for each <element> located by <selector> "<expression>" in <containerElement> with <timeoutSecs> second <wait|timeout>
  ```
  <p>Executes a step for each element in a list of elements in a container element in the current scope with a given lookup timeout.</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;step&gt;</code> is the DSL step or StepDef to execute for each element</li>
    <li><code>&lt;element&gt;</code> is the name that will be assigned to the current element occurrence (element is accessible in <code>&lt;step&gt;</code> by this name)</li>
    <li><code>&lt;selector&gt;</code> is the selector type, one of:
      <ul>
        <li><code>id</code> for selecting by id attribute</li>
        <li><code>name</code> for selecting by name attribute</li>
        <li><code>tag name</code> (or <code>tag</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.46.0">v2.46.0</Link>) for selecting by tag name</li>
        <li><code>css selector</code> (or <code>css</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.46.0">v2.46.0</Link>) for selecting by css expression</li>
        <li><code>class name</code> (or <code>class</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.46.0">v2.46.0</Link>) for selecting by class attribute</li>
        <li><code>xpath</code> for selecting by XPath</li>
        <li><code>link text</code> for selecting by link text</li>
        <li><code>partial link text</code> for selecting by partial link text</li>
        <li><code>javascript</code> (or <code>js</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.46.0">v2.46.0</Link>) for selecting <Link to="https://gweninterpreter.wordpress.com/2019/08/13/locating-web-elements-with-gwen/#byJavaScript">by JavaScript</Link></li>
      </ul>
    </li>
    <li><code>&lt;expression&gt;</code> is the selector expression returning one or many elements</li>
    <li><code>&lt;containerElement&gt;</code> is the name assigned to the container element</li>
    <li><code>&lt;timeoutSecs&gt;</code> is the timeout period in seconds</li>
    <li><code>&lt;wait|timeout&gt;</code> is either <code>wait</code> or <code>timeout</code></li>
  </ul>
  <p>Example</p>

  ```gherkin {7}
    Given the todo field can be located by class "new-todo"
      And the todo list can be located by class "todo-list"
      And the active count can be located by css ".todo-count strong"
     When I navigate to "https://todomvc.com/examples/react"
      And I enter "Walk the dog" in the todo field
      And I enter "Feed the cat" in the todo field
      And I tick todo item for each todo item located by class "toggle" in the todo list with 3 second wait
     Then the active count should be "0"
  ```

  <div class="grid-3">
    <div><Link to="#step-for-each-element-located-by-selector-expression-in-container-with-timeout">Link</Link></div>
    <div align="center"></div>
    <div align="right">Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.19.0">v2.19.0</Link></div>
  </div>
</details>

<details id="step-for-each-element-in-elements">
  <summary class="dsl">

  ```gherkin
  <step> for each <element> in <elements>
  ```
  <p>Executes a step for each element in a list of elements in the current scope with a default lookup timeout.</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;step&gt;</code> is the DSL step or StepDef to execute for each element</li>
    <li><code>&lt;element&gt;</code> is the name that will be assigned to the current element occurrence (element is accessible in <code>&lt;step&gt;</code> by this name)</li>
    <li><code>&lt;elements&gt;</code> is the name of the locator binding returning multiple elements</li>
  </ul>
  <p>Example</p>

  ```gherkin {7}
    Given the todo field can be located by class "new-todo"
      And the active count can be located by css ".todo-count strong"
      And all todo items can be located by css ".todo-list .toggle"
     When I navigate to "https://todomvc.com/examples/react"
      And I enter "Walk the dog" in the todo field
      And I enter "Feed the cat" in the todo field
      And I tick todo item for each todo item in all todo items
     Then the active count should be "0"
  ```

  <div class="grid-3">
    <div><Link to="#step-for-each-element-in-elements">Link</Link></div>
    <div align="center"></div>
    <div align="right">Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.4.0">v2.4.0</Link></div>
  </div>
</details>

<details id="step-for-each-data-record">
  <summary class="dsl">

  ```gherkin
  <step> for each data record
  ```
  <p>Executes a step for each record in a data table.</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;step&gt;</code> is the DSL step or StepDef to execute for each record</li>
    <li>Each field in a record can be accessed in <code>&lt;step&gt;</code> using the field's associated header name</li>
    <li>
      The following implicit bindings are available in <code>&lt;step&gt;</code>:
      <ul>
        <li><code>record.number</code> is the current record number (starting at 1)</li>
        <li><code>record.index</code> is the record index (starting at 0), since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.30.1">v2.30.1</Link></li>
      </ul>
    </li>
  </ul>
  <p>Example</p>
  
  <em>Feature</em>

  ```gherkin
    Scenario: my scenario
      Given I have the following active items
            | Item         |
            | Walk the dog |
            | Get the milk |
            | Feed the cat |
  ```

  <em>Meta</em>

  ```gherkin {7}
    @StepDef
    @DataTable
    Scenario: I have the following active items
      Given the todo field can be located by class "new-todo"
        And the active count can be located by css ".todo-count strong"
       When I navigate to "https://todomvc.com/examples/react"
        And I enter Item in the todo field for each data record
       Then the active count should be "3"
  ```

  <div class="grid-3">
    <div><Link to="#step-for-each-data-record">Link</Link></div>
    <div align="center"></div>
    <div align="right">Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.8.0">v2.8.0</Link></div>
  </div>
</details>

<details id="for-each-entry-in-text-ref-delimited-by">
  <summary class="dsl">

  ```gherkin
  <step> for each <entry> in <textRef> delimited by "<delimiter>"
  ```
  <p>Executes a step for each delimited text entry.</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;step&gt;</code> is the DSL step or StepDef to execute for each delimited entry</li>
    <li><code>&lt;entry&gt;</code> is the name that will be assigned to the current entry occurrence (entry is accessible in <code>&lt;step&gt;</code> by this name)</li>
    <li><code>&lt;textRef&gt;</code> is the name of the binding containing the delimitted values
      <ul>
        <li>Can be the name of any binding that contains or resolves to a delmited list of values, including a web element in which case the text in the element will be dynamically retrieved and used.</li>
      </ul>
    </li>
    <li><code>&lt;delimiter&gt;</code> the delimiter used in <code>&lt;textRef&gt;</code> to separate each value</li>
  </ul>
  <p>Example</p>

  ```gherkin {5}
    Given the todo field can be located by class "new-todo"
      And the active count can be located by css ".todo-count strong"
      And my items is "Walk the dog, Feed the cat, Get the milk"
     When I navigate to "https://todomvc.com/examples/react"
      And I enter todo item in the todo field for each todo item in my items delimited by ","
     Then the active count should be "3"
  ```

  <div class="grid-3">
    <div><Link to="#for-each-entry-in-text-ref-delimited-by">Link</Link></div>
    <div align="center"></div>
    <div align="right">Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.13.0">v2.13.0</Link></div>
  </div>
</details>

### Until/While

> Since [v3.48.0](https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v3.47.0), the following implicit attributes are available to <code>&lt;step&gt;</code>s:
> <ul>
>  <li><code>iteration.number</code> = current iteration starting at 1</li>
>  <li><code>iteration.index</code> = current iteration starting at 0</li>
> </ul>


<details id="step-until-or-while-condition">
  <summary class="dsl">

  ```gherkin
  <step> <until|while> <condition>
  ```
  <p>Repeatedly exectues a step until or while a condition is satisfied using a default delay and timeout period. The default delay between iterations is one tenth of the configured <code>gwen.web.wait.seconds</code> setting (or 1 second if not set). The default timeout period is 30 times the delay.</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;step&gt;</code> is the DSL step or StepDef to execute in each iteration</li>
    <li><code>&lt;until|while&gt;</code> is one of:
      <ul>
        <li><code>until</code> to repeat until the condition is satisfied</li>
        <li><code>while</code> to repeat while the condition is satisfied</li>
      </ul>
    </li>
    <li><code>&lt;condition&gt;</code> the name of a binding containing a javascript function or expression that will return true when the condition is satisfied and false when it is not.</li>
    <li>
      The following implicit binding is available in <code>&lt;step&gt;</code>:
      <ul>
        <li><code>iteration number</code> (or <code>iteration.number</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.52.0">v2.52.0</Link>) is the current iteration number (starting at 1)</li>
      </ul>
    </li>
  </ul>
  <p>Example</p>

  ```gherkin {13}
      Given the search field can be located by name "q"
        And the next page link can be located by id "pnnext"
        And topic is "what is gwen"
        And topic link can be located by partial link text "${topic}"
        And topic not found is defined by js
            """
            [...document.querySelectorAll("a")]
              .filter(a => a.textContent.includes('${topic}'))
              .length == 0
            """
       When I navigate to "https://google.com"
        And I enter "gwen interpreter" in the search field
        And I click the next page link while topic not found
        And I click topic link
       Then the page title should contain "${topic}"
  ```

  <div class="grid-3">
    <div><Link to="#step-until-or-while-condition">Link</Link></div>
    <div align="center"></div>
    <div align="right">Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v1.0.0">v1.0.0</Link></div>
  </div>
</details>

<details id="step-until-or-while-condition-using-delay">
  <summary class="dsl">

  ```gherkin
  <step> <until|while> <condition> using <delay> <delayUnit> delay
  ```
  <p>Repeatedly exectues a step until or while a condition is satisfied using the given delay interval and default timeout period. The default timeout period is 30 times the specified delay.</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;step&gt;</code> is the DSL step or StepDef to execute in each iteration</li>
    <li><code>&lt;until|while&gt;</code> is one of:
      <ul>
        <li><code>until</code> to repeat until the condition is satisfied</li>
        <li><code>while</code> to repeat while the condition is satisfied</li>
      </ul>
    </li>
    <li><code>&lt;condition&gt;</code> the name of a binding containing a javascript function or expression that will return true when the condition is satisfied and false when it is not.</li>
    <li><code>&lt;delay&gt;</code> is the delay period between steps repetitions</li>
    <li><code>&lt;delayUnit&gt;</code> is one of:
      <ul>
        <li><code>second</code></li>
        <li><code>millisecond</code></li>
      </ul>
    </li>
    <li>
      The following implicit binding is available in <code>&lt;step&gt;</code>:
      <ul>
        <li><code>iteration number</code> (or <code>iteration.number</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.52.0">v2.52.0</Link>) is the current iteration number (starting at 1)</li>
      </ul>
    </li>
  </ul>
  <p>Example</p>

  ```gherkin {13}
    Given the search field can be located by name "q"
        And the next page link can be located by id "pnnext"
        And topic is "what is gwen"
        And topic link can be located by partial link text "${topic}"
        And topic not found is defined by js "$('h3:contains("${topic}")').length == 0)"
            """
            [...document.querySelectorAll("a")]
              .filter(a => a.textContent.includes('${topic}'))
              .length == 0
            """
       When I navigate to "https://google.com"
        And I enter "gwen interpreter" in the search field
        And I click the next page link while topic not found using 1 second delay
        And I click topic link
       Then the page title should contain "${topic}"
  ```

  <div class="grid-3">
    <div><Link to="#step-until-or-while-condition-using-delay">Link</Link></div>
    <div align="center"></div>
    <div align="right">Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v1.7.0">v1.7.0</Link></div>
  </div>
</details>

<details id="step-until-or-while-condition-using-timeout">
  <summary class="dsl">

  ```gherkin
  <step> <until|while> <condition> using <timeout> <timeoutUnit> timeout
  ```
  <p>Repeatedly exectues a step until or while a condition is satisfied using a default delay and given timeout period. The default delay between iterations is one tenth of the configured gwen.web.wait.seconds setting (or 1 second if not set).</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;step&gt;</code> is the DSL step or StepDef to execute in each iteration</li>
    <li><code>&lt;until|while&gt;</code> is one of:
      <ul>
        <li><code>until</code> to repeat until the condition is satisfied</li>
        <li><code>while</code> to repeat while the condition is satisfied</li>
      </ul>
    </li>
    <li><code>&lt;condition&gt;</code> the name of a binding containing a javascript function or expression that will return true when the condition is satisfied and false when it is not.</li>
    <li><code>&lt;timeout&gt;</code> is the timeout period</li>
    <li><code>&lt;timeoutUnit&gt;</code> is one of:
      <ul>
        <li><code>minute</code></li>
        <li><code>second</code></li>
        <li><code>millisecond</code></li>
      </ul>
    </li>
    <li>
      The following implicit binding is available in <code>&lt;step&gt;</code>:
      <ul>
        <li><code>iteration number</code> (or <code>iteration.number</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.52.0">v2.52.0</Link>) is the current iteration number (starting at 1)</li>
      </ul>
    </li>
  </ul>
  <p>Example</p>

  ```gherkin {13}
    Given the search field can be located by name "q"
        And the next page link can be located by id "pnnext"
        And topic is "what is gwen"
        And topic link can be located by partial link text "${topic}"
        And topic not found is defined by js
            """
            [...document.querySelectorAll("a")]
              .filter(a => a.textContent.includes('${topic}'))
              .length == 0
            """
       When I navigate to "https://google.com"
        And I enter "gwen interpreter" in the search field
        And I click the next page link while topic not found using 15 second timeout
        And I click topic link
       Then the page title should contain "${topic}"
  ```

  <div class="grid-3">
    <div><Link to="#step-until-or-while-condition-using-timeout">Link</Link></div>
    <div align="center"></div>
    <div align="right">Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v1.7.0">v1.7.0</Link></div>
  </div>
</details>


<details id="step-until-or-while-condition-using-delay-and-timeout">
  <summary class="dsl">

  ```gherkin
  <step> <until|while> <condition> using <delay> <delayUnit> delay and <timeout> <timeoutUnit> timeout
  ```
  <p>Repeatedly exectues a step until or while a condition is satisfied using the given delay interval and timeout period.</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;step&gt;</code> is the DSL step or StepDef to execute in each iteration</li>
    <li><code>&lt;until|while&gt;</code> is one of:
      <ul>
        <li><code>until</code> to repeat until the condition is satisfied</li>
        <li><code>while</code> to repeat while the condition is satisfied</li>
      </ul>
    </li>
    <li><code>&lt;condition&gt;</code> the name of a binding containing a javascript function or expression that will return true when the condition is satisfied and false when it is not.</li>
    <li><code>&lt;delay&gt;</code> is the delay period between steps repetitions</li>
    <li><code>&lt;delayUnit&gt;</code> is one of:
      <ul>
        <li><code>second</code></li>
        <li><code>millisecond</code></li>
      </ul>
    </li>
    <li><code>&lt;timeout&gt;</code> is the timeout period</li>
    <li><code>&lt;timeoutUnit&gt;</code> is one of:
      <ul>
        <li><code>minute</code></li>
        <li><code>second</code></li>
        <li><code>millisecond</code></li>
      </ul>
    </li>
    <li>
      The following implicit binding is available in <code>&lt;step&gt;</code>:
      <ul>
        <li><code>iteration number</code> (or <code>iteration.number</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.52.0">v2.52.0</Link>) is the current iteration number (starting at 1)</li>
      </ul>
    </li>
  </ul>
  <p>Example</p>

  ```gherkin {13}
    Given the search field can be located by name "q"
        And the next page link can be located by id "pnnext"
        And topic is "what is gwen"
        And topic link can be located by partial link text "${topic}"
        And topic not found is defined by js
            """
            [...document.querySelectorAll("a")]
              .filter(a => a.textContent.includes('${topic}'))
              .length == 0
            """
       When I navigate to "https://google.com"
        And I enter "gwen interpreter" in the search field
        And I click the next page link while topic not found using 1 second delay and 5 second timeout
        And I click topic link
       Then the page title should contain "${topic}"
  ```

<details id="step-until-or-while-condition-using-no-delay-and-timeout">
  <summary class="dsl">

  ```gherkin
  <step> <until|while> <condition> using no delay and <timeout> <timeoutUnit> timeout
  ```
  <p>Repeatedly exectues a step until or while a condition is satisfied using no delay and the given timeout period.</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;step&gt;</code> is the DSL step or StepDef to execute in each iteration</li>
    <li><code>&lt;until|while&gt;</code> is one of:
      <ul>
        <li><code>until</code> to repeat until the condition is satisfied</li>
        <li><code>while</code> to repeat while the condition is satisfied</li>
      </ul>
    </li>
    <li><code>&lt;condition&gt;</code> the name of a binding containing a javascript function or expression that will return true when the condition is satisfied and false when it is not.</li>
    <li><code>&lt;timeout&gt;</code> is the timeout period</li>
    <li><code>&lt;timeoutUnit&gt;</code> is one of:
      <ul>
        <li><code>minute</code></li>
        <li><code>second</code></li>
        <li><code>millisecond</code></li>
      </ul>
    </li>
    <li>
      The following implicit binding is available in <code>&lt;step&gt;</code>:
      <ul>
        <li><code>iteration number</code> (or <code>iteration.number</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.52.0">v2.52.0</Link>) is the current iteration number (starting at 1)</li>
      </ul>
    </li>
  </ul>
  <p>Example</p>

  ```gherkin {13}
    Given the search field can be located by name "q"
        And the next page link can be located by id "pnnext"
        And topic is "what is gwen"
        And topic link can be located by partial link text "${topic}"
        And topic not found is defined by js
            """
            [...document.querySelectorAll("a")]
              .filter(a => a.textContent.includes('${topic}'))
              .length == 0
            """
       When I navigate to "https://google.com"
        And I enter "gwen interpreter" in the search field
        And I click the next page link while topic not found using no delay and 15 second timeout
        And I click topic link
       Then the page title should contain "${topic}"
  ```

  <div class="grid-3">
    <div><Link to="#step-until-or-while-condition-using-no-delay-and-timeout">Link</Link></div>
    <div align="center"></div>
    <div align="right">Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v1.7.0">v1.7.0</Link></div>
  </div>
</details>

<details id="step-until-or-while-condition-using-no-delay">
  <summary class="dsl">

  ```gherkin
  <step> <until|while> <condition> using no delay
  ```
  <p>Repeatedly exectues a step until or while a condition is satisfied using no delay and the default timeout period of 30 seconds.</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;step&gt;</code> is the DSL step or StepDef to execute in each iteration</li>
    <li><code>&lt;until|while&gt;</code> is one of:
      <ul>
        <li><code>until</code> to repeat until the condition is satisfied</li>
        <li><code>while</code> to repeat while the condition is satisfied</li>
      </ul>
    </li>
    <li><code>&lt;condition&gt;</code> the name of a binding containing a javascript function or expression that will return true when the condition is satisfied and false when it is not.</li>
    <li>
      The following implicit binding is available in <code>&lt;step&gt;</code>:
      <ul>
        <li><code>iteration number</code> (or <code>iteration.number</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.52.0">v2.52.0</Link>) is the current iteration number (starting at 1)</li>
      </ul>
    </li>
  </ul>
  <p>Example</p>

  ```gherkin {13}
    Given the search field can be located by name "q"
        And the next page link can be located by id "pnnext"
        And topic is "what is gwen"
        And topic link can be located by partial link text "${topic}"
        And topic not found is defined by js
            """
            [...document.querySelectorAll("a")]
              .filter(a => a.textContent.includes('${topic}'))
              .length == 0
            """
       When I navigate to "https://google.com"
        And I enter "gwen interpreter" in the search field
        And I click the next page link while topic not found using no delay
        And I click topic link
       Then the page title should contain "${topic}"
  ```

  <div class="grid-3">
    <div><Link to="#step-until-or-while-condition-using-no-delay">Link</Link></div>
    <div align="center"></div>
    <div align="right">Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v1.7.0">v1.7.0</Link></div>
  </div>
</details>

<details id="step-until-or-while-element-state">
  <summary class="dsl">

  ```gherkin
  <step> <until|while> <element> is[ not] <state>
  ```
  <p>Repeatedly exectues a step until or while an element is in a given state using a 1 second delay interval and 1 minute timeout period.</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;step&gt;</code> is the DSL step or StepDef to execute in each iteration</li>
    <li><code>&lt;until|while&gt;</code> is one of:
      <ul>
        <li><code>until</code> to repeat until the condition is satisfied</li>
        <li><code>while</code> to repeat while the condition is satisfied</li>
      </ul>
    </li>
    <li><code>&lt;element&gt;</code> is the name of the element to check the state of</li>
    <li><code>not</code> negates the state if included</li>
    <li><code>&lt;state&gt;</code> is one of:
      <ul>
        <li><code>displayed</code> to execute the step until or while the element is displayed</li>
        <li><code>hidden</code> to execute the step until or while the element is not displayed</li>
        <li><code>checked</code> or <code>ticked</code> to execute the step until or while a checkbox is ticked</li>
        <li><code>unchecked</code> or <code>unticked</code> to execute the step until or while a checkbox is not ticked</li>
        <li><code>enabled</code> to execute the step until or while the element is enabled</li>
        <li><code>disabled</code> to execute the step until or while the element is disabled</li>
      </ul>
    </li>
    <li>
      The following implicit binding is available in <code>&lt;step&gt;</code>:
      <ul>
        <li><code>iteration number</code> (or <code>iteration.number</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.52.0">v2.52.0</Link>) is the current iteration number (starting at 1)</li>
      </ul>
    </li>
  </ul>
  <p>Example</p>

  ```gherkin {5}
      Given the search field can be located by name "q"
        And the next page link can be located by id "pnnext"
       When I navigate to "https://google.com"
        And I enter "gwen interpreter" in the search field
        And I click the next page link while the next page link is displayed
       Then the next page link should not be displayed
  ```

  <div class="grid-3">
    <div><Link to="#step-until-or-while-element-state">Link</Link></div>
    <div align="center"></div>
    <div align="right">Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v3.44.0">v3.44.0</Link></div>
  </div>
</details>

<details id="step-until-or-while-element-state-using-delay">
  <summary class="dsl">

  ```gherkin
  <step> <until|while> <element> is[ not] <state> using <delay> <delayUnit> delay
  ```
  <p>Repeatedly exectues a step until or while an element is in a given state using the given delay interval and 1 minute timeout period.</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;step&gt;</code> is the DSL step or StepDef to execute in each iteration</li>
    <li><code>&lt;until|while&gt;</code> is one of:
      <ul>
        <li><code>until</code> to repeat until the condition is satisfied</li>
        <li><code>while</code> to repeat while the condition is satisfied</li>
      </ul>
    </li>
    <li><code>&lt;element&gt;</code> is the name of the element to check the state of</li>
    <li><code>not</code> negates the state if included</li>
    <li><code>&lt;state&gt;</code> is one of:
      <ul>
        <li><code>displayed</code> to execute the step until or while the element is displayed</li>
        <li><code>hidden</code> to execute the step until or while the element is not displayed</li>
        <li><code>checked</code> or <code>ticked</code> to execute the step until or while a checkbox is ticked</li>
        <li><code>unchecked</code> or <code>unticked</code> to execute the step until or while a checkbox is not ticked</li>
        <li><code>enabled</code> to execute the step until or while the element is enabled</li>
        <li><code>disabled</code> to execute the step until or while the element is disabled</li>
      </ul>
    </li>
    <li><code>&lt;delay&gt;</code> is the delay period between steps repetitions</li>
    <li><code>&lt;delayUnit&gt;</code> is one of:
      <ul>
        <li><code>second</code></li>
        <li><code>millisecond</code></li>
      </ul>
    </li>
    <li>
      The following implicit binding is available in <code>&lt;step&gt;</code>:
      <ul>
        <li><code>iteration number</code> (or <code>iteration.number</code> since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.52.0">v2.52.0</Link>) is the current iteration number (starting at 1)</li>
      </ul>
    </li>
  </ul>
  <p>Example</p>

  ```gherkin {5}
    Given the search field can be located by name "q"
        And the next page link can be located by id "pnnext"
       When I navigate to "https://google.com"
        And I enter "gwen interpreter" in the search field
        And I click the next page link until the next page link is not displayed using 3 second delay
       Then the next page link should not be displayed
  ```

  <p>Repeatedly exectues a step until or while an element is in a given state using a 1 second delay interval and given timeout period.</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;step&gt;</code> is the DSL step or StepDef to execute in each iteration</li>
    <li><code>&lt;until|while&gt;</code> is one of:

        <li><code>while</code> to repeat while the condition is satisfied</li>

    <li><code>&lt;state&gt;</code> is one of:
      <ul>
        <li><code>displayed</code> to execute the step until or while the element is displayed</li>
        <li><code>hidden</code> to execute the step until or while the element is not displayed</li>
        <li><code>checked</code> or <code>ticked</code> to execute the step until or while a checkbox is ticked</li>
        <li><code>unchecked</code> or <code>unticked</code> to execute the step until or while a checkbox is not ticked</li>
        <li><code>enabled</code> to execute the step until or while the element is enabled</li>
        <li><code>disabled</code> to execute the step until or while the element is disabled</li>
      </ul>
    </li>
    <li><code>&lt;timeout&gt;</code> is the timeout period</li>
    <li><code>&lt;timeoutUnit&gt;</code> is one of:
      <ul>
        <li><code>minute</code></li>
        <li><code>second</code></li>
        <li><code>millisecond</code></li>
      </ul>
    </li>

        <li><code>disabled</code> to execute the step until or while the element is disabled</li>
      </ul>
    </li>
    <li><code>&lt;delay&gt;</code> is the delay period between steps repetitions</li>

      <ul>
        <li><code>second</code></li>
        <li><code>millisecond</code></li>
      </ul>
    </li>
    <li><code>&lt;timeout&gt;</code> is the timeout period</li>
    <li><code>&lt;timeoutUnit&gt;</code> is one of:
      <ul>
        <li><code>minute</code></li>
        <li><code>second</code></li>
        <li><code>millisecond</code></li>
      </ul>
    </li>

### If

<details id="step-if-condition">
  <summary class="dsl">

  ```gherkin
  <step> if[ not] <condition>
  ```
  <p>Executes a step depending on whether or not a JS condition evaluates to true.</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;step&gt;</code> is the DSL step or StepDef to potentially execute</li>
    <li><code>not</code> negates the condition if included (Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v3.4.0">v3.4.0</Link>)</li>
    <li>
      <code>&lt;condition&gt;</code> the name of a binding containing a javascript function or expression that will return true or false
      <ul>
        <li>Since v3.14.1, the condition name cannot contain double qutoes</li>
      </ul>
    </li>
  </ul>
  <p>Example</p>

  ```gherkin {12,13}
    Given the search field can be located by name "q"
      And topic is "Automation Bindings"
      And topic link can be located by partial link text "${topic}"
      And topic found is defined by js
          """
          [...document.querySelectorAll("a")]
              .filter(a => a.textContent.includes('${topic}'))
              .length > 0
          """
     When I navigate to "https://google.com"
      And I enter "gwen automation" in the search field
      And I click topic link if topic found
     Then the page title should contain "${topic}" if topic found
  ```

  <div class="grid-3">
    <div><Link to="#step-if-condition">Link</Link></div>
    <div align="center"></div>
    <div align="right">Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v2.12.0">v2.12.0</Link></div>
  </div>
</details>

<details id="step-if-element-condition">
  <summary class="dsl">

  ```gherkin
  <step> if <element> is[ not] <state>
  ```
  <p>Executes a step depending on whether or not an element is in a given state.</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;step&gt;</code> is the DSL step or StepDef to potentially execute</li>
    <li><code>&lt;element&gt;</code> is the name of the element to check the state of</li>
    <li><code>not</code> negates the state if included</li>
    <li><code>&lt;state&gt;</code> is one of:
      <ul>
        <li><code>displayed</code> to execute the step if the element is displayed</li>
        <li><code>hidden</code> to execute the step if the element is not displayed</li>
        <li><code>checked</code> or <code>ticked</code> to execute the step if a checkbox is ticked</li>
        <li><code>unchecked</code> or <code>unticked</code> to execute the step if a checkbox is not ticked</li>
        <li><code>enabled</code> to execute the step if the element is enabled</li>
        <li><code>disabled</code> to execute the step if the element is disabled</li>
      </ul>
    </li>
  </ul>
  <p>Example</p>

  ```gherkin {6}
    Given the search field can be located by name "q"
      And topic is "Automation"
      And topic link can be located by partial link text "${topic}"
     When I navigate to "https://google.com"
      And I enter "gwen automation" in the search field
      And I click topic link if topic link is displayed
     Then the page title should contain "${topic}"
  ```

  <div class="grid-3">
    <div><Link to="#step-if-element-condition">Link</Link></div>
    <div align="center"></div>
    <div align="right">Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v3.33.0">v3.33.0</Link></div>
  </div>
</details>

<details id="step-if-binding-defined">
  <summary class="dsl">

  ```gherkin
  <step> if <attribute> is[ not] defined
  ```
  <p>Executes a step depending on whether or not an attribute is bound in the global or current scope.</p>
  </summary>
  <p>Where</p>
  <ul>
    <li><code>&lt;step&gt;</code> is the DSL step or StepDef to potentially execute</li>
    <li><code>&lt;attribute&gt;</code> is the name of the attribute to check</li>
    <li><code>not</code> include to execute step if attribute is not bound</li>
  </ul>
  <p>Example</p>

  Given the CSV file: lookup/StateCodes.csv

  ```csv {3}
  Code,Name
  ACT,Australian Capital Territory
  NSW,New South Wales
  NT,Northern Territory
  QLD,Queensland
  SA,South Australia
  TAS,Tasmania
  VIC,Victoria
  WA,Western Australia
  ```

  The following will bind "New South Wales" in the 2nd record to <code>state name</code> in the global scope
  ```gherkin {3}
   Given the state code is "UNKNOWN"
    When I lookup Name in the "lookup/StateCodes.csv" file as state name where "'${data.record.Code}' == '${the state code}'"
    Then unresolved is "true" if state name is not defined
  ```

  <div class="grid-3">
    <div><Link to="#step-if-binding-defined">Link</Link></div>
    <div align="center"></div>
    <div align="right">Since <Link to="https://github.com/gwen-interpreter/gwen-web/releases/tag/v3.33.0">v3.33.0</Link></div>
  </div>
</details>
